## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Cherry-pick revert of Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusions (#168157)

**Repository:** github.com/sg-benchmarks/pytorch--ca246612 (mirror of pytorch)
**Difficulty:** HARD
**Category:** cross_module_bug_fix



## Description

This is a cherry-pick of the revert of PR #168157, which added `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass.

PR #168157 introduced pattern matching in the Inductor compiler to fuse activation functions (ReLU, GELU) with Addmm (matrix multiply + bias add) operations into a single `_addmm_activation` call that leverages cuBLASLt's fused epilogue support. This optimization aimed to reduce kernel launches and memory traffic for common `Linear -> Activation` patterns.

However, the fusion caused regressions in certain model configurations and needed to be reverted. This cherry-pick applies the revert to the release branch, undoing:
- The `_addmm_activation` pattern replacement in Inductor's lowering/decomposition passes
- The associated pattern matcher registrations for ReLU(Addmm) and GELU(Addmm)
- Any cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths added for these patterns

Changes:
- 4 files modified
- 93 additions, 87 deletions

## Task

Implement the fix: Cherry-pick revert of Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusions

Description: Revert PR #168157 which added `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass for cuBLASLt fused epilogue support. The fusion caused regressions and needs to be reverted.

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import os

from torch._inductor import pattern_matcher
from torch._inductor.fx_passes import joint_graph, post_grad


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Start by deleting all the existing patterns.
    for path in pattern_matcher.SERIALIZED_PATTERN_PATH.iterdir():
        if path.name in {"__init__.py", "__pycache__"}:
            continue
        if path.is_file():
            path.unlink()

    # Now have joint_graph load all known patterns and tell the pattern matcher
    # to serialize the patterns as it goes.
    os.environ["PYTORCH_GEN_PATTERNS"] = "1"
    joint_graph.lazy_init()

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import os

from torch._inductor import pattern_matcher
from torch._inductor.fx_passes import joint_graph


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Start by deleting all the existing patterns.
    for path in pattern_matcher.SERIALIZED_PATTERN_PATH.iterdir():
        if path.name in {"__init__.py", "__pycache__"}:
            continue
        if path.is_file():
            path.unlink()

    # Now have joint_graph load all known patterns and tell the pattern matcher
    # to serialize the patterns as it goes.
    os.environ["PYTORCH_GEN_PATTERNS"] = "1"
    joint_graph.lazy_init()

   685→@functools.cache
   686→def register_addmm_activation_fusions():
   687→    def is_valid_addmm_activation_fusion(match: Match) -> bool:
   688→        # Exclude ROCm
   689→        if torch.version.hip:
   690→            return False
   691→
   692→        if config.max_autotune or config.max_autotune_gemm:
   693→            return False
   694→
   695→        inp = match.kwargs["inp"].meta["val"]
   696→
   697→        if not inp.is_cuda:
   698→            return False
   699→
   700→        output = match.output_node()
   701→        return not all(
   702→            is_pointwise_use(use, lambda target: torch.Tag.reduction in target.tags)
   703→            for use in output.users
   704→        )
   705→
   706→    args = [torch.empty(3), torch.empty(4, 2), torch.empty(2, 3)]
   707→    beta_alpha_workaround = {"beta": 1.3, "alpha": 1.2}
   708→
   709→    def addmm_relu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
   710→        return aten.relu(aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha))
   711→
   712→    def addmm_gelu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
   713→        return aten.gelu(
   714→            aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha), approximate="tanh"
   715→        )
   716→
   717→    def addmm_relu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
   718→        return aten._addmm_activation(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha)

   720→    def addmm_gelu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
   721→        return aten._addmm_activation(
   722→            inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha, use_gelu=True
   723→        )

   713→def reorder_for_locality(graph: torch.fx.Graph):

   715→
   716→        def check():
   717→            # This is a wait node, and `other_node`` is some collective node.
   718→            # Eager semantics allow waits to be issued in a different order than
   719→            # the collectives. Reordering this wait node might reorder collectives
   720→            # which cause hangs. Once we have SPMD mode, we can safely reorder them.
   721→            # However, increasing the locality between a collective and its wait node
   722→            # is generally worse for performance.
   723→            return node.target != torch.ops._c10d_functional.wait_tensor.default
   724→    else:
   725→

   727→            return True

Otherwise, all dependent\n        constructor nodes won't be moved.\n\n        - target: target device type\n        - allow_outputs: allow outputs to be moved\n        - allow_inputs: allow inputs to be moved\n        \"\"\"\n\n        self.target = target\n        self.allow_inputs = allow_inputs\n        self.allow_outputs = allow_outputs\n\n        assert isinstance(target, str), (\n            \"target should be a string representing the device type. \"\n            f\"Got: {type(target).__name__}\"\n        )\n\n    def allow_cpu_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node that returns a tensor on the target device may have\n        cpu tensors as input.\n        \"\"\"\n        return node.target in (\n            torch.ops.aten.index.Tensor,\n            torch.ops.aten.index_put.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.index_put_.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.copy.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.copy_.default,\n            torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        node_device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        return node_device is not None and node_device.type == self.target\n\n    def is_cpu_scalar_tensor(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is a cpu scalar tensor.\n        \"\"\"\n        device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        is_cpu = device is not None and device.type == \"cpu\"\n        ten = node.meta.get(\"val\")\n        is_scalar = isinstance(ten, torch.Tensor) and len(ten.size()) == 0\n        return is_cpu and is_scalar\n\n    def all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node's inputs are either cpu scalar tensors or\n        on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        inputs = (\n            inp\n            for inp in itertools.chain(node.args, node.kwargs.values())\n            if isinstance(inp, fx.Node)\n        )\n        return all(\n            self.is_cpu_scalar_tensor(inp) or target device.\n\n        If this function returns False, it means that this node and all of its users\n        won't be moved into the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        if node.target ==        ):\n            return True\n\n        if is_index_put_and_requires_h2d_sync_for_gpu_value(node):\n            return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def get_node_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> torch.device | None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the device of a node.\n        \"\"\"\n        ten = node.meta.get(\"val\")\n        return None if not isinstance(ten, torch.Tensor) else ten.device\n\n    def get_cpu_indeg_count(self, graph: fx.Graph) -> dict[fx.Node, int]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the number of cpu inputs to a node\n        \"\"\"\n        cpu_indeg: gpu_node,\n                        lambda x: x\n                        not in [cpu_concat, gpu_concat, gpu_split, gpu_node]\n                        + unsqueezed_nodes\n                        and which constructors cannot be moved to gpu\n        cannot_move_to_gpu = OrderedSet[fx.Node]()\n\n        # For any node in the graph, which constructors does it have a dependency on\n        constructor_dependencies: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = defaultdict(\n            OrderedSet\n        )\n\n        # could use union find but not worth complexity here\n            set1.update(set2)\n            for obj in set1:\n                equal_constructor_sets[obj] = set1\n            return set1\n\n        queue: list[fx.Node] = list(constructors)\n\n        for c in queue:\n            constructor_dependencies[c].add(c)\n\n        while queue:\n            node = queue.pop()\n            dependencies = constructor_dependencies[node]\n\n            for user in node.users:\n                if self.cannot_be_moved(user):\n                    cannot_move_to_gpu.update(dependencies)\n                    break\n\n                # this node takes only cpu scalar tensors or gpu tensors as inputs\n                    # and outputs a gpu tensor. we can convert its cpu scalar inputs to gpu\n                    # without making further changes\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                else:\n                    # otherwise, we should continue look at its downstream uses\n                    cpu_indeg[user] -= 1\n                    if cpu_indeg[user] == 0:\n                        del cpu_indeg[user]\n                        queue.append(user)\n\n                unioned_set = make_dependencies_equivalent(\n                    dependencies, constructor_dependencies[user]\n                )\n                constructor_dependencies[user] = unioned_set\n\n        for node in cpu_indeg:\n            if constructor_dependencies[node]:\n                cannot_move_to_gpu.update(constructor_dependencies[node])\n\n        all_cannot_move_to_gpu = cannot_move_to_gpu.copy()\n        for constructor in cannot_move_to_gpu:\n            all_cannot_move_to_gpu.update(equal_constructor_sets[constructor])\n\n        return OrderedSet(constructors) - all_cannot_move_to_gpu\n\n\ndef move_constructors_to_gpu(graph: fx.Graph) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Moves intermediary tensors which are constructed on the cpu to gpu when safe\n    \"\"\"\n\n    # #!/usr/bin/env python3
import os

from torch._inductor import pattern_matcher
from torch._inductor.fx_passes import joint_graph


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Start by deleting all the existing patterns.
    for path in pattern_matcher.SERIALIZED_PATTERN_PATH.iterdir():
        if path.name in {"__init__.py", "__pycache__"}:
            continue
        if path.is_file():
            path.unlink()

    # Now have joint_graph load all known patterns and tell the pattern matcher
    # to serialize the patterns as it goes.
    os.environ["PYTORCH_GEN_PATTERNS"] = "1"
    joint_graph.lazy_init()

@functools.cache
def register_addmm_activation_fusions():
    def is_valid_addmm_activation_fusion(match: Match) -> bool:
        # Exclude ROCm
        if torch.version.hip:
            return False

        if config.max_autotune or config.max_autotune_gemm:
            return False

        inp = match.kwargs["inp"].meta["val"]

        if not inp.is_cuda:
            return False

        output = match.output_node()
        return not all(
            is_pointwise_use(use, lambda target: torch.Tag.reduction in target.tags)
            for use in output.users
        )

    args = [torch.empty(3), torch.empty(4, 2), torch.empty(2, 3)]
    beta_alpha_workaround = {"beta": 1.3, "alpha": 1.2}

    def addmm_relu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten.relu(aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha))

    def addmm_gelu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten.gelu(
            aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha), approximate="tanh"
        )

    def addmm_relu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten._addmm_activation(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha)

    def addmm_gelu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten._addmm_activation(
            inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha, use_gelu=True
        )

    patterns = (addmm_relu_pattern, addmm_gelu_pattern)
    replacements = (addmm_relu_replacement, addmm_gelu_replacement)
    for pattern, replacement in zip(patterns, replacements):
        key = f"{pattern.__name__}"
        gen_register_replacement(
            key,
            # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]
            pattern,
            # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]
            replacement,
            args,
            # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]
